Not all\n1255: // claims are necessarily allocated yet, so here we can set the SuitableNodes\n1256: // field for those which are pending.\n1257: func (pl *dynamicResources) PreScore(ctx context.Context, cs *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*framework.NodeInfo) *framework.Status {\n1258: \tif !pl.enabled {\n1259: \t\treturn nil\n1260: \t}\n1261: \tstate, err := getStateData(cs)\n1262: \tif err != nil {\n1263: \t\treturn statusError(klog.FromContext(ctx), err)\n1264: \t}\n1265: \tdefer func() {\n1266: \t\tstate.preScored = true\n1267: \t}()\n1268: \tif len(state.claims) == 0 {\n1269: \t\treturn nil\n1270: \t}\n1271: \n1272: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n1273: \tpending := false\n1274: \tfor index, claim := range state.claims {\n1275: \t\tif claim.Status.Allocation == nil &&\n1276: \t\t\tstate.informationsForClaim[index].controller == nil {\n1277: \t\t\tpending = true\n1278: \t\t\tbreak\n1279: \t\t}\n1280: \t}\n1281: \tif !pending {\n1282: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"no pending claims with control plane controller\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n1283: \t\treturn nil\n1284: \t}\n1285: \n1286: \tif haveAllPotentialNodes(state.podSchedulingState.schedulingCtx, nodes) {\n1287: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"all potential nodes already set\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"potentialnodes\", klog.KObjSlice(nodes))\n1288: \t\treturn nil\n1289: \t}\n1290: \n1291: \t// Remember the potential nodes. The object will get created or\n1292: \t// updated in Reserve. This is both an optimization and\n1293: \t// covers the case that PreScore doesn't get called when there\n1294: \t// is only a single node.\n1295: \tlogger.V(5).Info(\"remembering potential nodes\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"potentialnodes\", klog.KObjSlice(nodes))\n1296: \tnumNodes := len(nodes)\n1297: \tif numNodes > resourcev1alpha2.PodSchedulingNodeListMaxSize {\n1298: \t\tnumNodes = resourcev1alpha2.PodSchedulingNodeListMaxSize\n1299: \t}\n1300: \tpotentialNodes := make([]string, 0, numNodes)\n1301: \tif numNodes == len(nodes) {\n1302: \t\t// Copy all node names.\n1303: \t\tfor _, node := range nodes {\n1304: \t\t\tpotentialNodes = append(potentialNodes, node.Node().Name)\n1305: \t\t}\n1306: \t} else {\n1307: \t\t// Select a random subset of the nodes to comply with\n1308: \t\t// the PotentialNodes length limit. Randomization is\n1309: \t\t// done for us by Go which iterates over map entries\n1310: \t\t// randomly.\n1311: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--11602f08@49a089c8038dde44833da37a0472396aafc25ab1/-/blob/pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go%3FL1200-1310"}}}

It registers events for `ResourceClaimParameters`, `ResourceClassParameters`, `ResourceClaim`, `PodSchedulingContext`, `Node`, and `ResourceClass` — but **not `ResourceSlice`**. When a DRA driver starts after pod creation and publishes ResourceSlice objects, no event is sent to the scheduling queue to retry the pod.\n\n### Part 3 — Missing informer handler\n- **File**: pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go\n- **Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n- **Line**: ~395–543 (the switch statement)\n- **Explanation**: Even if `ResourceSlice` were registered in `EventsToRegister()`, `addAllEventHandlers()` would need a `case framework.ResourceSlice:` branch to wire up the actual informer event handler. The resource model is empty.\n\n**Step 3: Filter marks all nodes unsuitable**\n\n`dynamicResources.Filter()` calls `state.informationsForClaim[index].controller.nodeIsSuitable(ctx, node.Name, state.resources)`. With an empty resource model, all nodes fail the check and return Unschedulable.\n\n**Step 4: Pod lands in unschedulable queue**\n\n`ScheduleOne()` records the failure reasons and moves the pod to the unschedulable pod pool. The scheduling queue tracks *which plugin rejected the pod* and *which cluster events* can make it schedulable again (from `EventsToRegister()`).\n\n**Step 5: Driver starts and creates ResourceSlices — but nothing happens**\n\nWhen the DRA driver finally starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects via the Kubernetes API, an informer event fires. However:\n\n1. **No informer handler is registered** for ResourceSlice events in `addAllEventHandlers()` — the switch statement has no `case framework.ResourceSlice:` branch.\n2. **No event is registered** in `dynamicResources.EventsToRegister()` for `ResourceSlice` Add/Update events — so the scheduling queue doesn't know that ResourceSlice events should trigger re-evaluation of pods rejected by the DRA plugin.\n\nEven if the informer fired an event, the scheduling queue's `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` would not move the stuck pod because it would have no record of any plugin having registered interest in ResourceSlice events.\n\n**Step 6: Pod remains permanently Pending**\n\nWithout any triggering event to move the pod from unschedulable → active queue, it stays stuck indefinitely. The only way it would be retried is via the periodic \"flush unschedulable pods\" timer (typically 5 minutes), which is a poor user experience and is the wrong mechanism for this case.\n\n### Why This Is Specifically a Bug\n\nAll other DRA-related resources that the scheduler watches (`ResourceClaim`, `ResourceClass`, `ResourceClaimParameters`, `ResourceClassParameters`, `PodSchedulingContext`) correctly have:\n1. A GVK constant in `framework/types.go`\n2. An entry in `EventsToRegister()` in the DRA plugin\n3. A handler in `addAllEventHandlers()` in `eventhandlers.go`\n\n`ResourceSlice` — despite being actively used during scheduling via `pl.resourceSliceLister` — is missing from all three places, making it a completely invisible object from the scheduler's event-driven perspective.\nEOF\necho \"Solution written successfully\""},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":106,"cache_read_input_tokens":50298,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":106,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"9667dceb-ed84-4351-8f7b-4ab69569dd06","uuid":"aa77a17f-f3cd-41cb-a2b9-ec2433ff5be8"}

A GVK constant in `framework/types.go`\n2. An entry in `EventsToRegister()` in the DRA plugin\n3. A case handler in `addAllEventHandlers()` in `eventhandlers.go`\n\n`ResourceSlice` — despite being actively fetched during scheduling via `pl.resourceSliceLister` (line 356 in `dynamicresources.go`) and being the primary source of device availability information — is missing from all three places, making it completely invisible to the scheduler's event-driven re-queuing architecture.\n\nThe race condition described in the bug report is thus: if the driver starts *before* the pod, ResourceSlices already exist when `PreFilter` runs so scheduling succeeds immediately. If the pod arrives *before* the driver, scheduling fails and the pod enters the unschedulable queue — but the subsequent ResourceSlice creation events that would fix the situation are never wired up to trigger a retry.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":374,"cache_read_input_tokens":53030,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":374,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":7,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"9667dceb-ed84-4351-8f7b-4ab69569dd06","uuid":"1c2eb966-1dd7-46b4-b088-3bb69ba93441"}

This is the foundational omission that makes everything else impossible.\n\n### Part 2 — Missing EventsToRegister entry\n- **File**: pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Line**: ~386–412\n- **Explanation**: The DRA plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method lists the cluster events that should cause the scheduler to re-evaluate unschedulable pods rejected by this plugin. It registers events for `ResourceClaimParameters`, `ResourceClassParameters`, `ResourceClaim`, `PodSchedulingContext`, `Node`, and `ResourceClass` — but **not `ResourceSlice`**. When a DRA driver starts after pod creation and publishes ResourceSlice objects, no event is sent to the scheduling queue to retry the pod.\n\n### Part 3 — Missing informer handler\n- **File**: pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go\n- **Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n- **Line**: ~395–543 (the switch statement)\n- **Explanation**: Even if `ResourceSlice` were registered in `EventsToRegister()`, `addAllEventHandlers()` would need a `case framework.ResourceSlice:` branch to wire up the actual informer event handler. Without this, the GVK would fall through to the `default:` branch which tries to parse it as a dot-separated dynamic GVK string — and since `\"ResourceSlice\"` has no dots, it would be silently skipped (the `strings.Count(string(gvk), \".\") < 2` check at line 529 would filter it out with a logged error).\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n```diff\n--- a/pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go\n+++ b/pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go\n@@ -93,6 +93,7 @@ const (\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n\n--- a/pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go\n+++ b/pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go\n@@ -408,6 +408,10 @@ func (pl *dynamicResources) EventsToRegister() []framework.ClusterEventWithHint\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// A pod might be waiting for ResourceSlices to appear (e.g. when the DRA driver\n+\t\t// starts after the pod was created). Adding or updating a ResourceSlice may make\n+\t\t// previously unschedulable pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n }\n\n--- a/pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go\n+++ b/pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go\n@@ -491,6 +491,15 @@ func addAllEventHandlers(\n \t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n**Step 1: Pod requests DRA device, driver not yet running**\n\nWhen a pod with a `ResourceClaim` using structured parameters is created, `ScheduleOne()` in `schedule_one.go` begins a scheduling cycle.\n\n**Step 2: PreFilter populates resource model from empty ResourceSlice lister**\n\n`dynamicResources.PreFilter()` calls `newResourceModel()` in `structuredparameters.go:51`:\n```go\nslices, err := resourceSliceLister.List(labels.Everything())\n```\nSince the DRA driver hasn't started yet, no ResourceSlices exist. The resource model is empty — no node has any available devices.\n\n**Step 3: Filter marks all nodes unsuitable**\n\n`dynamicResources.Filter()` at line ~1138 calls `state.informationsForClaim[index].controller.nodeIsSuitable(ctx, node.Name, state.resources)`. With an empty resource model, every node fails the device availability check and the plugin returns Unschedulable for all nodes.\n\n**Step 4: Pod lands in unschedulable queue**\n\n`ScheduleOne()` records the failure reasons and moves the pod to the unschedulable pod pool. The scheduling queue tracks *which plugin rejected the pod* and *which cluster events* (from `EventsToRegister()`) can make it reschedulable.\n\n**Step 5: Driver starts and creates ResourceSlices — but nothing happens**\n\nWhen the DRA driver finally starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, an informer event fires. However:\n\n1. **No informer handler is registered** for ResourceSlice events in `addAllEventHandlers()` — the switch statement has no `case framework.ResourceSlice:` branch. There is no GVK constant to match against, so no case is ever reached.\n2. **No event is registered** in `dynamicResources.EventsToRegister()` for ResourceSlice Add/Update events — so even if an event arrived, the scheduling queue doesn't know it should trigger re-evaluation of pods rejected by the DRA plugin.\n\nThe combined effect: ResourceSlice creation events are completely invisible to the scheduler's re-queuing mechanism.\n\n**Step 6: Pod remains permanently Pending**\n\nWithout any triggering event to move the pod from unschedulable → active queue, it stays stuck indefinitely. The only escape is the periodic \"flush unschedulable pods\" timer (default 5 minutes), which is neither timely nor correct behavior for this scenario.\n\n### Why This Is Specifically a Bug\n\nAll other DRA-related resources that the scheduler watches (`ResourceClaim`, `ResourceClass`, `ResourceClaimParameters`, `ResourceClassParameters`, `PodSchedulingContext`) correctly have:\n1. A GVK constant in `framework/types.go`\n2. An entry in `EventsToRegister()` in the DRA plugin\n3. A case handler in `addAllEventHandlers()` in `eventhandlers.go`\n\n`ResourceSlice` — despite being actively fetched during scheduling via `pl.resourceSliceLister` (line 356 in `dynamicresources.go`) and being the primary source of device availability information — is missing from all three places, making it completely invisible to the scheduler's event-driven re-queuing architecture.\n\nThe race condition described in the bug report is thus: if the driver starts *before* the pod, ResourceSlices already exist when `PreFilter` runs so scheduling succeeds immediately. If the pod arrives *before* the driver, scheduling fails and the pod enters the unschedulable queue — but the subsequent ResourceSlice creation events that would fix the situation are never wired up to trigger a retry.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
